Amazing thought provoking writing and I read this book about once every three to four years, it is definitely therapeutic and insightful!<br />Read or watch any of Dr. Wayne Dyers publicatio</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_379535972">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379535972" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/57844-delnavaa" class="left imgcol" title="Delnavaa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432458343p2/57844.jpg" alt="Delnavaa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/379535972?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/57844-delnavaa" class="user" title="Delnavaa">Delnavaa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer379535972">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2454982836807940098">honestly, I don't know why it received a 3 star rating. This book changed my outlook! Dyre teaches us that Approval seeking is engrained in our culture. Some feel guilt and shame and are constantly seeking approval doubting themselves and not being able to decide or process their feelings to acheive compromise or a rational result. They value peoples opinions more than they value their own especially if those people they seek approval of are close and important to them. This develops at a very y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2454982836807940098">honestly, I don't know why it received a 3 star rating. This book changed my outlook! Dyre teaches us that Approval seeking is engrained in our culture. Some feel guilt and shame and are constantly seeking approval doubting themselves and not being able to decide or process their feelings to acheive compromise or a rational result. They value peoples opinions more than they value their own especially if those people they seek approval of are close and important to them. This develops at a very young age. It has to do with self-worth yes, but it develops at school, in our culture, from our parents attitudes. The best thing about this book is it gives you a very nice little test to take to determine which areas you really need to work on, Approval, Self-Love, Perfectionism, etc... I would recommend this book to anyone who has always doubted their own abilities and struggle with dependency and reliance on others to make their decisions for them. It teaches you how to disarm people who criticize you and makes you realize that people have different experiences, right or wrong. If you open yourself up to negativity, to vulnerability, then most people will tend to dump their insecurities on you. It teaches you to accept responsibility for your actions, to stop worrying about the future, to live in the now, and to stop saying sorry and apologizing for every single thing, mistake or not! One more thing, stop asking this or that person if your judgement is right or wrong. Think it through, write the negatives and positives (pros and cons) of feeling the way you do and then rationalize it. This will stop your impulsive behaviour to lash out. You think relationship books helps? THEY DON'T! These books do! If you want to have a meaningful relationship, start by building yourself, by accepting your mistakes, but not beating yourself up for it. The more you think positively, the more radiant and attractive you feel, and the more assertive your behaviour will be. Let me say that I am stating the obvious, and it is easier said than done! But running a marathon will probably be easier than changing your self-defeating habits. It will take time, take focus, (read Think Fast Think Slow) and it will take a lot of verbatim with yourself. Don't expect others to help you along the way, to seek marriage in order to seek security, to seek love for the sake of running away from your problems. The end result is disastrous! Seek instead self-love, self-worth, and accept people for who they are, accept what they say but never internalize it. you never know what people are really thinking, and you can never truly trust a person's judgement until you trust your own first! It is a book I will read and re-read and re-read! The one thing to keep in mind is that you need not only to read but to practice the things you've learned. So stop beating yourself up, compromise, disarm those who feed your negativity, and rationalize by taking nothing personally and start living your life the way you want and stop worrying about what others think of you. Accept love, stop fearing the outcomes, predict nothing, and enjoy every single minute! I hope this helps! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2454982836807940098">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer220339835">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7825567919426340185">This book just makes a lot of sense. It completely blew my mind! Herein, Dyer presents us with a completely different paradigm, a new lens from which to look at ourselves and the world. He introduces very many fundamental principles on right living, most of which we are already aware of, but unwilling to apply or fear the consequences of doing so - being that we live in a society wherein we are constantly bombarded on a daily basis with hundreds of cultural messages that encourages us to obey, t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7825567919426340185">This book just makes a lot of sense. It completely blew my mind! Herein, Dyer presents us with a completely different paradigm, a new lens from which to look at ourselves and the world. He introduces very many fundamental principles on right living, most of which we are already aware of, but unwilling to apply or fear the consequences of doing so - being that we live in a society wherein we are constantly bombarded on a daily basis with hundreds of cultural messages that encourages us to obey, to conform, to think and behave a certain way, to blame, to seek approval &amp; acceptance, to feel guilt, etc. I'm giving myself time digest everything I've read, the paradigm shift I've experienced, then read the book AGAIN before attempting a "proper" review of this amazing piece of work.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer63509156">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8338419480048033926">I love Wayne Dyer so when I was helping my MIL clear out and organize her huge book collection and found this old gem, I asked if I could have it. Let me tell you, it does not disappoint. Written in 1976 and his first book, it reads like he wrote it last week. Straight forward and real, this book will hit home for everyone! I'm going slow and learning, learning.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6168161237833522401"><br />Fantastic! I read it when I was still a teen and then I have read it again a few years ago. The best book of its kind. All those new cheesy, overly simplistic authors who are proclaming they 'know how to find happiness and will take you there'and are now at Harvard delivering subjects on 'Happiness', should probably learn from Dyer. That said, Dyer's writing style has changed and I don't enjoy his actual work as much as I enjoyed his early work...but I don't buy 'happiness' books anymore, anyway</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6168161237833522401"><br />Fantastic! I read it when I was still a teen and then I have read it again a few years ago. The best book of its kind. All those new cheesy, overly simplistic authors who are proclaming they 'know how to find happiness and will take you there'and are now at Harvard delivering subjects on 'Happiness', should probably learn from Dyer. That said, Dyer's writing style has changed and I don't enjoy his actual work as much as I enjoyed his early work...but I don't buy 'happiness' books anymore, anyway.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/713606433?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22649679-bob" class="user" title="Bob">Bob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer713606433">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer235651640510953190"><br /><br />Your Erroneous Zones is simply one of the greatest self-help books ever written. For people just beginning to read self-help or spiritual books, this book is a great place to start. It is nearly imperative that if one reads any book by Dr. Wayne Dyer that they start with this book. By reading his books in order of copyright, the amazing shift in his philosophy and interests over the years can be witnessed. <br /><br />Dr. Dyer has written so many books, but important books to follow with this one are "Pulli</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText235651640510953190"><br /><br />Your Erroneous Zones is simply one of the greatest self-help books ever written. For people just beginning to read self-help or spiritual books, this book is a great place to start. It is nearly imperative that if one reads any book by Dr. Wayne Dyer that they start with this book. By reading his books in order of copyright, the amazing shift in his philosophy and interests over the years can be witnessed. <br /><br />Dr. Dyer has written so many books, but important books to follow with this one are "Pulling Your Own Strings," "Your Sacred Self," and "Manifest Your Destiny." Later works include "Change Your Thoughts - Change Your Life: Living the Wisdom of the Tao." <br /><br />Your Erroneous Zones is a book for people who are just beginning to discover that we all have thoughts that do not serve us towards living a self-fulfilled life. We are given erroneous viewpoints from childhood and can live a more self-actualized life by becoming aware of our self-defeating thoughts.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.returnoftheway.com/" target="_blank">http://www.returnoftheway.com/</a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="235651640510953190">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer278604777">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14694234078781433502">Aunque por lo general no disfruto mucho de leer libros considerados de auto-ayuda, este libro logró atraparme con su objetividad y su realismo, me encantó la forma en que se ejemplifican las zonas erróneas con casos de la vida real, debo admitir que me sentí identificado con bastantes zonas erróneas en las que debo trabajar. Lo recomiendo mucho para cualquier persona.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1275529214">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1275529214" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4859940-tara-brabazon" class="left imgcol" title="Tara Brabazon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442456675p2/4859940.jpg" alt="Tara Brabazon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1275529214?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4859940-tara-brabazon" class="user" title="Tara Brabazon">Tara Brabazon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1275529214">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer693334789700621381">This book is O.K. It attempts to correct and manage a culture of excuses. It is a book about the self - about how the individual can activate thoughts and agency to transform their life. The problem is that the book is a context-free zone. In other words, no matter what an individual may experience, it can be changed by thinking differently about it.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this is an inaccurate assumption. Certainly, there are solid elements of self empowerment in this book. But the understanding of powe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText693334789700621381">This book is O.K. It attempts to correct and manage a culture of excuses. It is a book about the self - about how the individual can activate thoughts and agency to transform their life. The problem is that the book is a context-free zone. In other words, no matter what an individual may experience, it can be changed by thinking differently about it.<br /><br />Unfortunately, this is an inaccurate assumption. Certainly, there are solid elements of self empowerment in this book. But the understanding of power and injustice is absent. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="693334789700621381">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1040225656">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1040225656" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8391431-m-j" class="left imgcol" title="M. J."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1332730259p2/8391431.jpg" alt="M. J." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1040225656?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 20, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8391431-m-j" class="user" title="M. J.">M. J.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8391431-m-j?shelf=read-non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">read-non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1040225656">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10254037416022449483">I admit to being skeptical of this book before I began. I needed a non-fiction book of some sort to balance my reading diet, and this one had somehow found its way into our bedroom and been staring at me from the dresser for--well, I suspect several years--so I decided I would at least see what it said. I expected it to be a lot of psychobabble pablum of little value. It was so much worse than that.<br /><br />It hit me wrong twice within the first few pages. First, it made the argument that since we are mo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10254037416022449483">I admit to being skeptical of this book before I began. I needed a non-fiction book of some sort to balance my reading diet, and this one had somehow found its way into our bedroom and been staring at me from the dresser for--well, I suspect several years--so I decided I would at least see what it said. I expected it to be a lot of psychobabble pablum of little value. It was so much worse than that.<br /><br />It hit me wrong twice within the first few pages. First, it made the argument that since we are mortal we have only our brief life on earth and therefore should base everything we do on making that as good, in our own view, as we can. Obviously, if he is right then much of what he says follows from it--but I am of the view that this life is just the opening chapter of eternity, and that what we do now matters in eternal terms. I thus had a bad start right there.<br /><br />He then attempted to commandeer the word "intelligence" to mean something other than intelligence. Certainly I can understand that people who are not intelligent can still be wise and smart and clever and capable and successful--indeed, more successful than I. I understand that intelligence, as measured by tests and puzzles and logic problems, is not the be-all and end-all of existence. However, as a person for whom intelligence is perhaps my strongest trait it was offensive to be told that such a thing does not really exist. The author suggested that since anyone can learn anything if he works at it hard and long enough, everyone is really as intelligent as anyone else. Right. Tell it to Einstein.<br /><br />Gradually I began to get the overall theory of the book. People are unhappy in large part because we let other people dictate our view of our selves and our actions. If you want to be happy, you must ignore everything everyone else thinks--peer pressure, parental guidance, schooling, everything you have ever learned, everything society tells you about how you ought to act. In short, you should decide what you want to do and who you want to be, then do that, and not worry about what anyone else thinks.<br /><br />That seems to me to be the definition of sociopathic.<br /><br />He tries to avoid that by hedging here and there. You should not do things simply because everyone else disapproves--doing something for its shock value is just as much being controlled by others as doing things for approval. Ultimately, though, the lines are ephemeral, the boundaries nonexistent, and the direction for finding a happy life is simply to do whatever you want and ignore anyone else who suggests that you are making bad choices.<br /><br />I'm not one for social and societal correctness; I'm pretty bad at it, actually. However, I do perceive major problems with a concept of ignoring the dictates of society. It is bound to interfere with your happiness, whether because it results in exclusion from social gatherings or in incarceration and criminal penalties. The author just assumes that his readers will not go there, without any clear explanation of why.<br /><br />Now, I am probably not the right audience for this book. It was a bestseller, and probably found its audience among middle and upper middle class businessmen and housewives and others--people whose problems in life are mostly that they are stressed about little things. People with real problems in the real world are not going to benefit much from this--the advice that worry has no value probably won't be much use to someone who is certain that he will be evicted or have his car repossessed or his utilities terminated, and he has no means of forestalling it. Of course it has no value; yet the advice to live life as it comes is not very encouraging to those for whom life comes at you fast, as the insurance commercial said.<br /><br />So maybe it would be helpful for some people, but frankly I did not find it to be advice I would apply in my own life or recommend to others--at least, in the main. Here and there I thought there was something of worth, but it was buried in material I would as soon not have read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10254037416022449483">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/4191081-barbara?shelf=non-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">non-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152315282">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13227509880279208038">This is the very first "inspirational" or "personal growth" book I read. I read it when I was a senior at the University of Miami and I was taking an inter-personal communications course, and we were required to give a presentation on a book that may have changed our life in some way. I absolutely loved this book, and to this day I still love Wayne Dyer's philosophy. I think a lot of the information in this book may be outdated now (or maybe not), but Wayne has written so many books since this o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13227509880279208038">This is the very first "inspirational" or "personal growth" book I read. I read it when I was a senior at the University of Miami and I was taking an inter-personal communications course, and we were required to give a presentation on a book that may have changed our life in some way. I absolutely loved this book, and to this day I still love Wayne Dyer's philosophy. I think a lot of the information in this book may be outdated now (or maybe not), but Wayne has written so many books since this one, and I've found that his thoughts have evolved greatly since he wrote this. I may pick up a copy of this just to flip through it and see exactly how much he has changed since he wrote this. But for now, I would say that anyone who needs a good shot of inspiration and/or motivation to make some major life changes (and/or changes in your way of thinking about things), would benefit greatly from any of Wayne Dyer's books. Actually, he has such a great speaking voice, I would recommend trying out any of his audio books.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38596897" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/59506-printable-tire" class="left imgcol" title="Printable Tire"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226430554p2/59506.jpg" alt="Printable Tire" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/38596897?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 24, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/59506-printable-tire" class="user" title="Printable Tire">Printable Tire</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38596897">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12298623078931635274">While I admit if you fostered every single piece of advice in this book you'd probably become a big fat smelly bore (or like cousin Larry when he took that self-help class on Perfect Strangers), I did find this book rather stimulating and honest. I haven't read any other self-help books that I can think of (other than maybe Quarterlife Crisis and Hero with a Thousand Faces) and I found Dyer's book surprisingly thoughtful, insightful, literary and incredibly not stupid. He is sometimes contradict</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12298623078931635274">While I admit if you fostered every single piece of advice in this book you'd probably become a big fat smelly bore (or like cousin Larry when he took that self-help class on Perfect Strangers), I did find this book rather stimulating and honest. I haven't read any other self-help books that I can think of (other than maybe Quarterlife Crisis and Hero with a Thousand Faces) and I found Dyer's book surprisingly thoughtful, insightful, literary and incredibly not stupid. He is sometimes contradictory and vague, and I see that as a great compliment to a self-help book. I was surprised to realize I've already eliminated most of my erroneous zones, except for dependency. It's been a long time since I read Kant but Dyer's advice seems to fall into that "speak the truth at all times" category. Might get you a punch in the face every once in a while.<br />My favorite part of the book was the rearranging of song titles/lyrics into "personal mastery rather than approval seeking" terms, seeing as 99.9% of all songs are about expressing needy emotions (I'm looking at you, emo). His examples are pretty funny. See if you can match the new title with the original song (keep in mind he wrote the book in the 70's):<br />-I make myself feel like a natural woman; it has nothing to do with you.<br />-I choose to love you. I must have wanted to do it then, but now I've changed my mind.<br />-People who need people are the unluckiest people in the world. But people who want, love, and enjoy people are making themselves happy.<br />-I make myself so very happy because of the things I tell myself about you.<br />-I am the sunshine of my life, and having you in it makes it even brighter.<br />-I can stop loving you, but at this point I chose not to.<br /><br />Not as catchy as the original titles, I guess. Still a fun parlor game or something to do when you're bored in your car.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12298623078931635274">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer879686261">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14069726652297570747">Self-help books are a low-cost, important tool for individuals who have the will to change and are able to use the prescription with discernment, courage and tenacity. Of course, that's always easier said than done, especially in a world where enculturation is highly promoted and individualism discouraged. I read Your Erroneous Zones years ago and just finished rereading it. Both times, I found it to be helpful. In it, Wayne Dyer candidly explains our negative thought processes, the payoffs for</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14069726652297570747">Self-help books are a low-cost, important tool for individuals who have the will to change and are able to use the prescription with discernment, courage and tenacity. Of course, that's always easier said than done, especially in a world where enculturation is highly promoted and individualism discouraged. I read Your Erroneous Zones years ago and just finished rereading it. Both times, I found it to be helpful. In it, Wayne Dyer candidly explains our negative thought processes, the payoffs for hanging onto them, and a prescription for change and effective living.<br /><br />Being an artist, I've always approached life with a healthy portion of curiosity, and societies rules with cautionary rebellion. That's not to say worries and uncertainty are not present, but if we allow all the "What ifs" to immobilize us, then sadly how much regret and resentment we are sure to own at the end of our journey.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1408462760">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1408462760?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/34130752-mar-a-greene" class="user" title="María Greene">María Greene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/357886.Your_Erroneous_Zones" title="Paperback 9780061091483" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/34130752-mar-a-greene?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1408462760">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3979838365153833069">Aunque sé que muchos odian este libro (y probablemente por pura moda), yo encuentro que es UNA MARAVILLA. Tiene razón ¡en tantas cosas! En todo, prácticamente, diría... yo lo leí cuando chica, y después hace poco, y lo encuentro muy certero, y además está escrito con tanta claridad, y los ejemplos son tan gráficos que, en medio de lo trágicas que son algunas cosas, a uno se le sale la carcajada. A mí nunca se me va a olvidar, por ejemplo, la supuesta imagen de la persona a quien uno no ayuda a l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3979838365153833069">Aunque sé que muchos odian este libro (y probablemente por pura moda), yo encuentro que es UNA MARAVILLA. Tiene razón ¡en tantas cosas! En todo, prácticamente, diría... yo lo leí cuando chica, y después hace poco, y lo encuentro muy certero, y además está escrito con tanta claridad, y los ejemplos son tan gráficos que, en medio de lo trágicas que son algunas cosas, a uno se le sale la carcajada. A mí nunca se me va a olvidar, por ejemplo, la supuesta imagen de la persona a quien uno no ayuda a llevar las bolsas del supermercado, que se cae por las escaleras y se muere por culpa de uno, jajaja. La persona que baja las bolsas sin avisar, claro y que lo luego culpa a uno por eso. Es una forma de manipulación, dicho sea de paso... el ejemplo es muy bueno.<br /><br />Creo que este libro es muy útil, para la vida. Explica todo con claridad, peras con manzanas y no solo permite que uno mejore sus errores, sino que también permite leer mejor a los demás, y así defenderse mejor de cuando nos pasan a llevar. Y permite tener menos resentimientos porque uno, en vez de enojarse (tanto), comprende, y tiene compasión porque se da cuenta de que los otros nos hacen sufrir solo porque ellos también sufren, se equivocan con ellos mismos y con el resto, igual que nosotros.<br /><br />Es un texto muy revelador. Una pena que el género autoayuda tenga tan mala fama, porque realmente marca una diferencia. A mí realmente creo que me hizo una mejor persona y que no solo yo le debo cosas, sino que la gente a mi alrededor y, a su vez, la gente alrededor suyo, jajaja.<br /><br />Así que lo recomiendo, mucho. Incluso está entre mis favs. Y a mucha honra.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a href="/book/show/709528.Tus_zonas_err_neas" title="Paperback 9780307274069" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21484353-fausto?shelf=libro-electronico" class="actionLinkLite">libro-electronico</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21484353-fausto?shelf=psicologia" class="actionLinkLite">psicologia</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer987621365">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5511264262079650124">Ha sido mi 1º libro de autoayuda y no ha estado nada mal, y además tiene párrafos interesantes. Por lo menos no es aburrido, y se pueden sacar varios consejos útiles. <br /><br />Lo importante para conseguir la autoconfianza, la felicidad, y eliminar esas zonas erróneas, es tener fuerza de voluntad y espíritu de sacrificio. Algo que por otra parte es elemental y básico para afrontar cualquier problema.<br />Uno de los asuntos principales es analizar los diversos comportamientos negativos, como son: la culpa, el r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5511264262079650124">Ha sido mi 1º libro de autoayuda y no ha estado nada mal, y además tiene párrafos interesantes. Por lo menos no es aburrido, y se pueden sacar varios consejos útiles. <br /><br />Lo importante para conseguir la autoconfianza, la felicidad, y eliminar esas zonas erróneas, es tener fuerza de voluntad y espíritu de sacrificio. Algo que por otra parte es elemental y básico para afrontar cualquier problema.<br />Uno de los asuntos principales es analizar los diversos comportamientos negativos, como son: la culpa, el remordimiento, la preocupación, la frustración, la ira, etc. Y después detalla cuáles son sus causas externas, como nos afectan y que comportamientos son recomendables para eliminarlos. <br />Muy sugestivas y didácticas son las críticas a la cultura, la educación, las relaciones familiares, el estado o la religión sobre la influencia que tienen para controlar la forma de pensar y nuestro comportamiento.<br /><br />También destaco las actitudes positivas que fomenta, como la autoestima (aunque echo en falta un poco de autocrítica), la independencia sobre el pensamiento de los demás, atreverse a conocer nuevas experiencias, vivir el presente (el carpe diem de los romanos) o aceptar la realidad tal como es.<br /><br />Es recomendable, y conviene repasar los capítulos o fragmentos que cada uno crea que le puedan servir. Ayuda a afrontar con una perspectiva positiva varias cuestiones y dificultades.<br /><br />Mi nota: 6.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6CsdXd/NAW/viH22Cv1O+oh62O7Skan4ES1CliOb4I6N/yKOLR8VlWNQCQ10nKhIwY0b95tM7lJ7JEcE7w4Wyw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2960.Wayne_W_Dyer">About Wayne W. Dyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/2960.Wayne_W_Dyer"><img alt="2960" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1231508105p2/2960.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5211082986912509790">Wayne Walter Dyer was a popular American self-help advocate, author and lecturer. His 1976 book Your Erroneous Zones has sold over 30 million copies and is one of the best-selling books of all time. It is said to have "[brought] humanistic ideas to the masses".<br /><br />He received his D.Ed. degree in counseling from Wayne State University. He was a guidance counselor in Detroit at the high school level and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5211082986912509790">Wayne Walter Dyer was a popular American self-help advocate, author and lecturer. His 1976 book Your Erroneous Zones has sold over 30 million copies and is one of the best-selling books of all time. It is said to have "[brought] humanistic ideas to the masses".<br /><br />He received his D.Ed. degree in counseling from Wayne State University. He was a guidance counselor in Detroit at the high school level and a professor of counselor education at St. John's University in New York.<br />He first pursued an academic career, publishing in journals and running a successful private therapy practice, but his lectures at St. John's, which focused on positive thinking and motivational speaking techniques, attracted students beyond those enrolled. A literary agent persuaded Dyer to package his ideas in book form, resulting in Your Erroneous Zones; although initial sales were thin, Dyer quit his teaching job and began a publicity tour of the United States, doggedly pursuing bookstore appearances and media interviews ("out of the back of his station wagon", according to Michael Korda, making the best-seller lists "before book publishers even noticed what was happening"</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5211082986912509790">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1447132-your-erroneous-zones">Quotes from Your Erroneous Zones</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
